# 1000 Expert Prompts
### The Ultimate Collection of Battle-Tested ChatGPT & Claude Prompts for Serious Professionals

> **10 categories. 1000 prompts. Zero fluff.** Every prompt is role-based, variable-driven, and framework-powered — so you get boardroom-quality output on the first run.

---

## Who This Is For

- **Founders & operators** who want strategy-consultant output without the retainer
- **Marketers & copywriters** who need conversion-grade copy in minutes, not weeks
- **Engineers & product leads** who want principal-level code review and architecture guidance
- **Creators** who need viral hooks, editorial-grade edits, and platform-native content
- **Anyone tired of "write me a blog post" prompts** that produce forgettable slop

## What Makes These Different

Most prompt packs are generic one-liners: *"Write me a marketing email."* Useless. These are engineered with the four pillars of high-leverage prompting:

1. **Role specificity** — Every prompt anchors the model to a concrete expert ("a senior direct-response copywriter who has written $100M+ in control-beating sales letters") so you get that expert's mental model, not an average of the internet.
2. **Named frameworks** — StoryBrand, JTBD, Blue Ocean, AIDA, PAS, Hexagonal Architecture, DDD, CQRS, SOLID, Hero's Journey, Skyscraper, E-E-A-T, STAR, GROW. Real frameworks from real practitioners.
3. **Concrete variables** — Fill in `[PRODUCT]`, `[AUDIENCE]`, `[PRICE]`, `[COMPETITOR]` and the prompt does the rest. No guessing what the model needs.
4. **Defined output structure** — Every prompt ends with "Output as..." so you get a table, diagram, outline, or numbered list — not a wall of text.

## How to Use This Book

1. **Pick a category** from the Table of Contents.
2. **Find a prompt** that matches your task (each prompt has a clear title).
3. **Replace the `[BRACKETS]`** with your own inputs (product, audience, numbers, URLs).
4. **Paste into ChatGPT-4o, Claude 3.5 Sonnet, Gemini 1.5 Pro, or any frontier model.**
5. **Iterate** — most prompts ask clarifying questions or produce multiple options so you can refine.

**Pro tip:** Prompts in categories 4 (Software), 5 (AI/Automation), and 8 (Data) often work best when you paste code, data, or logs alongside them.

## Legal & License

- You get an **unlimited personal + commercial license** to use these prompts in your work.
- You **may not** resell, repackage, or redistribute the pack itself (or a meaningful portion of it) as your own product.
- No warranty. AI output requires human review — especially for legal, medical, and financial use cases.

## 1 — Marketing, Sales & Copywriting
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> Brand positioning · sales letters · VSLs · Meta & Google ads · email sequences · pricing psychology · cold outbound · discovery calls · objection handling · VOC mining

---


### 1. Brand Positioning Statement Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a brand strategist who has led positioning for 3 unicorn SaaS companies. Using the Geoffrey Moore positioning framework, craft a positioning statement for [PRODUCT] serving [AUDIENCE] against [COMPETITOR]. Ask me 5 clarifying questions first about category, primary differentiator, proof points, and emotional payoff. Then output: (1) the full "For/Who/Is a/That/Unlike/Our product" statement, (2) 3 alternate versions ranked by boldness, and (3) a 1-sentence boardroom pitch.

### 2. Category Design Blueprint
**Prompt**: Act as a category designer trained in the Play Bigger methodology. For [PRODUCT] in the [INDUSTRY] space, design a new category that reframes the problem away from existing competitors. Analyze the current category's constraints, name a new category with POV (point of view), and output: category name, POV manifesto (3 paragraphs), lightning strike launch idea, and the 5 words customers should associate with us. Include a "category king" test checklist.

### 3. Jobs-To-Be-Done Interview Script
**Prompt**: Act as a JTBD researcher trained by Bob Moesta and Clay Christensen. Write a 45-minute customer interview script for [PRODUCT] that uncovers the functional, emotional, and social jobs buyers hire it for. Include the 4 forces timeline (push, pull, anxiety, habit), first-thought moments, and switch triggers. Output as: (1) opening rapport questions, (2) timeline excavation questions, (3) force-mapping questions, (4) closing synthesis, and (5) red flags to listen for.

### 4. StoryBrand BrandScript Generator
**Prompt**: Act as a certified StoryBrand guide. Build a complete BrandScript for [COMPANY] selling [PRODUCT] to [AUDIENCE]. Fill every section of Donald Miller's 7-part framework: Character (customer), Problem (external/internal/philosophical), Guide (empathy + authority), Plan (3 steps), Call to Action (direct + transitional), Success, and Failure stakes. Output as a labeled table, then translate it into a 150-word homepage headline + subhead + CTA button copy.

### 5. Blue Ocean Strategy Canvas
**Prompt**: Act as a Blue Ocean strategist from INSEAD. Create a Strategy Canvas for [PRODUCT] against the top 3 competitors in [MARKET]. Apply the Four Actions Framework (Eliminate, Reduce, Raise, Create) to identify uncontested market space. Output: (1) current competing factors scored 1-10 per competitor, (2) ERRC grid, (3) new value curve description, (4) the "tagline test" one-liner that captures the new offering. Include one contrarian move most competitors would reject.

### 6. Message-Market Fit Audit
**Prompt**: Act as a messaging strategist who has run 50+ April Dunford-style positioning workshops. Audit the current messaging for [PRODUCT] at [URL]. Score it 1-10 on: clarity of who it's for, differentiated value, proof, competitive alternatives named, and "so what" test. Identify the #1 messaging gap costing conversions. Output as a table with Score/Evidence/Fix columns, then rewrite the hero section headline + subhead using the Dunford "not X, but Y" pattern.

### 7. Brand Voice Codification
**Prompt**: Act as a brand voice strategist who built voice guides for Mailchimp and Oatly. Given 5 samples of [COMPANY]'s existing copy (I will paste), codify the brand voice into a reusable guide. Output: (1) 4 voice dimensions on a slider (e.g., Formal-Casual), (2) "We are / We are not" list of 10 pairs, (3) vocabulary do/don't list, (4) 3 tone variations (educate, sell, apologize) with examples, (5) a 50-word voice test paragraph writers can copy-calibrate against.

### 8. Value Proposition Canvas Fill
**Prompt**: Act as a Strategyzer-certified business coach. Complete a full Value Proposition Canvas for [PRODUCT] targeting [CUSTOMER_SEGMENT]. On the customer side: 5 jobs, 5 pains ranked by severity, 5 gains ranked by relevance. On the value map: pain relievers, gain creators, products/services. Then score the fit 1-10 and identify the weakest pain-reliever match. Output as two labeled columns, plus a "fit gap" paragraph with the one feature or message to develop next.

### 9. Differentiation Axis Finder
**Prompt**: Act as a positioning consultant trained by April Dunford. For [PRODUCT] competing against [COMPETITOR_1] and [COMPETITOR_2], identify 3 credible differentiation axes that aren't "better features." Consider: ideal customer segment, use case specialization, integration depth, speed of value, pricing model, support philosophy. Output a 2x2 perceptual map placing us + competitors, plus a 75-word "why we're different" narrative using the strongest axis. Flag any axis that would bait a race-to-the-bottom.

### 10. Manifesto Writing Framework
**Prompt**: Act as a brand copywriter who has written manifestos for Apple, Nike, and Patagonia-level brands. Write a 250-word manifesto for [COMPANY] that articulates why we exist, what we stand against, and who we're fighting for. Use short declarative sentences, contrast ("we believe X, not Y"), and one unifying battle cry. Output: (1) the full manifesto, (2) the 7-word boardroom version, (3) the 3 "enemy" concepts we reject. Do not use generic words like "innovative," "passion," or "journey."

### 11. Long-Form Sales Letter Scaffold
**Prompt**: Act as a senior direct-response copywriter who has written $100M+ in control-beating sales letters for Agora and Boardroom. Draft a 3,000-word sales letter for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE] targeting [AUDIENCE]. Use the Gary Halbert 19-step structure: attention-grabbing headline, deck copy, story lead, problem agitation, unique mechanism, offer, bonuses, guarantee, scarcity, P.S. Include 3 headline variations above the letter and specify where to split-test. Output as a fully formatted draft with section labels.

### 12. VSL Script (10-Minute)
**Prompt**: Act as a VSL scriptwriter who has produced videos generating $50M+ in sales. Write a 10-minute video sales letter for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]. Use the Russ Henneberry VSL structure: pattern interrupt hook, big promise, credibility stack, problem story, solution reveal, mechanism proof, offer stack, price justification, risk reversal, urgency, CTA. Output as a 2-column script (visual/voiceover) with timestamps every 60 seconds. Include a "hook A/B test" with 3 alternate opens.

### 13. Landing Page Conversion Rewrite
**Prompt**: Act as a CRO copywriter with 200+ winning A/B tests for SaaS landing pages. I'll paste a URL or copy. Rewrite it using the Joanna Wiebe "message hierarchy" method: top of page = most unaware, bottom = most ready. Apply the 5-second clarity test and the "one idea per section" rule. Output: (1) new hero headline + subhead + CTA, (2) 5 section headings in order, (3) social proof placement map, (4) objection section, (5) a checklist of 7 CRO fixes ranked by expected lift.

### 14. PAS Sales Page Opener
**Prompt**: Act as a direct-response copywriter trained in the Dan Kennedy school. Write 5 different Problem-Agitate-Solve openers (150 words each) for a sales page selling [PRODUCT] to [AUDIENCE]. Each opener should use a different emotional hook: fear, frustration, embarrassment, ambition, injustice. Output as a numbered table with columns: Hook Emotion / Opener Copy / Best For. End with the recommendation on which opener to lead with and why, based on audience temperature.

### 15. Headline Formula Stack
**Prompt**: Act as a headline copywriter who has studied every winning Agora control. Generate 25 headlines for [PRODUCT] serving [AUDIENCE] using these proven formulas: (1) How to X without Y, (2) The secret of X, (3) Who else wants X, (4) X ways to Y, (5) Warning: X, (6) If you X, you can Y, (7) Little known ways to X, (8) Give me X and I'll Y, (9) X mistakes X makes, (10) The lazy person's way to X. Output as a table with Formula / Headline / Predicted CTR (low/med/high) / Rationale.

### 16. Unique Mechanism Creator
**Prompt**: Act as a direct-response strategist trained by Stefan Georgi and Justin Goff. Create a proprietary "unique mechanism" name and explanation for why [PRODUCT] works when others fail. The mechanism should feel scientific, proprietary, and name-able (e.g., "The 3-Phase Collagen Cascade"). Output: (1) 5 mechanism name candidates, (2) the winning mechanism's 200-word explanation with 3 credibility anchors, (3) how to insert it into a sales page lead, (4) FTC-safe hedging language to avoid overclaiming.

### 17. Guarantee Design Workshop
**Prompt**: Act as an offer strategist who has designed guarantees for Alex Hormozi-level offers. Design 3 guarantee options for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]: (1) standard money-back, (2) conditional outcome-based, (3) better-than-risk-free "pay us if it works." For each, specify refund terms, fraud protection, expected refund rate, and psychological strength score 1-10. Output as a comparison table plus the exact copy block to insert in the sales page. Flag legal language to run by counsel.

### 18. Testimonial Mining Framework
**Prompt**: Act as a VOC researcher who builds social proof for conversion-optimized landing pages. Given [RAW_TESTIMONIAL_TEXT], extract the 5 most persuasive snippets using the "Specific > Emotional > Believable" filter. For each snippet, identify which objection it overcomes (price, effort, credibility, results, fit). Output as a table with Quote / Objection Countered / Placement Suggestion (hero, pricing, CTA, etc.). Then write a 50-word "featured testimonial" combining the best elements, formatted for hero placement.

### 19. Pricing Page Copy Rewrite
**Prompt**: Act as a SaaS pricing page copywriter who has lifted conversion 40%+ on Pipedrive-scale accounts. Rewrite the pricing page for [PRODUCT] with 3 tiers. For each tier, write: tier name (outcome-based, not "Pro"), 1-sentence positioning, price + billing note, 5 benefit bullets (not features), decoy effect on middle tier, CTA microcopy. Output as a 3-column table. Then add a 100-word "which plan is right for you" comparison block and 3 FAQs addressing pricing objections.

### 20. Above-The-Fold Stress Test
**Prompt**: Act as a landing page conversion specialist from CXL. Stress-test the above-the-fold section of [URL] against the 10-point MECLABS clarity rubric: value proposition clarity, exclusivity, credibility, friction, anxiety, motivation, alignment, relevance, eye-path, mobile fold. Score each 1-5 with evidence and prescribe the single highest-ROI fix. Output as a scored rubric table, then deliver the rewritten hero as: eyebrow / H1 / subhead / trust strip / primary CTA / secondary CTA. Include one bold contrarian suggestion.

### 21. 7-Day Welcome Email Sequence
**Prompt**: Act as a lifecycle email strategist who has built 6-figure welcome sequences for info-product brands. Write a 7-email welcome sequence for new [PRODUCT] subscribers. Map each email to: Day 0 (deliver lead magnet + origin story), Day 1 (core belief), Day 2 (big problem), Day 3 (soft sell), Day 4 (case study), Day 5 (objection handling), Day 6 (hard sell with deadline). Output each email with subject line, preview text, 150-250 word body, P.S., and CTA. Include 2 subject line variations per email.

### 22. Re-Engagement Winback Campaign
**Prompt**: Act as an email retention strategist who has reactivated 6-figure lists for Shopify brands. Design a 4-email winback campaign for subscribers inactive 90+ days on [LIST]. Use this arc: Email 1 (curiosity "did we do something wrong?"), Email 2 (value bomb, no ask), Email 3 (best-of highlights), Email 4 (goodbye + last-chance offer). Output each with subject line, preview, body, CTA. Include the segmentation SQL/filter logic, send-time recommendation, and the unsubscribe threshold to stop.

### 23. Launch Email Sequence (Pre/During/Post)
**Prompt**: Act as a launch copywriter who has run 7-figure Jeff Walker PLF campaigns. Write a 9-email launch sequence for [PRODUCT] launching on [DATE] at [PRICE]. Map: 3 pre-launch (PLC1 opportunity, PLC2 transformation, PLC3 experience), 3 open-cart (cart opens, social proof, objections), 3 close-cart (24 hours, 6 hours, 1 hour). Output each with subject, preview, 200-word body, CTA. Include the scarcity mechanic and one "bonus unlock" trigger mid-campaign. Label emotional tone per email.

### 24. Nurture Sequence For Cold Leads
**Prompt**: Act as a B2B SaaS lifecycle marketer. Build a 10-email nurture sequence for cold leads who downloaded [LEAD_MAGNET] but haven't booked a demo. Use the "Education-Insight-Case Study-Soft CTA-Hard CTA" pattern across 4 weeks. Each email must deliver one tactical insight before any pitch. Output as a table with columns: Day / Subject / Preview / Core Insight / CTA / Goal. Then write Email 1 and Email 5 in full (300 words each). Include the tag/segment logic to enter and exit the sequence.

### 25. Cart Abandonment Flow (Ecom)
**Prompt**: Act as an ecommerce email strategist who runs Klaviyo flows for 8-figure DTC brands. Build a 5-email abandoned cart sequence for [STORE] selling [PRODUCT_TYPE] at [AOV]. Timing: 1 hour, 4 hours, 24 hours, 48 hours, 72 hours. Include: reminder, social proof, FAQ/objection buster, discount offer (only if AOV > $X), last chance. Output each email with subject, preview, hero image direction, 100-word body, CTA. Flag which email to A/B test and the expected recovery rate benchmark.

### 26. Subject Line A/B Test Bank
**Prompt**: Act as an email copywriter who has split-tested 5,000+ subject lines. For [EMAIL_TOPIC] to [AUDIENCE], generate 20 subject lines across 5 psychological categories (4 each): curiosity gap, self-interest, social proof, urgency, personal/story. Each line must be under 45 characters. Output as a table with: Category / Subject Line / Character Count / Predicted Open Rate Tier (Hi/Med/Lo) / Why It Works. Then recommend the top 2 to test against and the control subject line to beat.

### 27. Broadcast Email Weekly Framework
**Prompt**: Act as a creator economy email strategist who has grown newsletters to 100k+ subscribers. Design a repeatable weekly broadcast template for [NEWSLETTER] in the [NICHE] niche. Output: (1) weekly section structure (hook, main lesson, tool/link, community shoutout, CTA), (2) word count targets per section, (3) editorial calendar themes for 4 weeks, (4) 3 evergreen subject line templates, (5) one growth loop to ask subscribers to share. Include a "don't do this" list of 5 newsletter killers.

### 28. Post-Purchase Email Sequence
**Prompt**: Act as a CX email strategist for premium digital products. Write a 6-email post-purchase sequence for buyers of [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]. Goals: maximize consumption, reduce refunds, drive reviews, trigger upsell. Map: Email 1 (welcome + access), Email 2 (quick win), Email 3 (milestone check-in), Email 4 (case study), Email 5 (review ask), Email 6 (upsell to [NEXT_PRODUCT]). Output each with subject, preview, 200-word body, CTA, and send-time. Include refund-rate reduction rationale.

### 29. Newsletter Lead Magnet Funnel
**Prompt**: Act as a lead gen strategist who builds high-converting lead magnet funnels. Design a complete funnel to turn a [LEAD_MAGNET_TOPIC] into 1,000 subscribers/month for [AUDIENCE]. Output: (1) lead magnet title + 3 alternatives using the "Ultimate/Blueprint/Cheat Sheet" frameworks, (2) opt-in page copy (headline, subhead, 3 bullets, CTA, trust line), (3) thank-you page upsell, (4) first 3 nurture emails, (5) paid traffic ad hook. Specify opt-in conversion benchmark to aim for.

### 30. Email Deliverability Copy Audit
**Prompt**: Act as an email deliverability expert who has rescued suspended SendGrid accounts. Audit the last [X] emails from [SENDER] for spam trigger language, link density, image/text ratio, and subject line red flags. Output: (1) spam score per email (1-10), (2) list of trigger words detected, (3) rewrite of the worst offender, (4) 5-point sender reputation action plan, (5) "safe word" replacements for common flags (e.g., "free," "guarantee," "100%"). Include Gmail Postmaster benchmarks.

### 31. Meta Ad Copy (5 Angles)
**Prompt**: Act as a Meta ads copywriter who has managed $10M+ in DTC ad spend. For [PRODUCT] at [PRICE] targeting [AUDIENCE], write 5 primary text variations (125 words max each) using 5 different angles: (1) problem-aware pain, (2) transformation story, (3) contrarian take, (4) social proof reel, (5) direct offer. Each must pass the "scroll-stop first line" test. Output as a table with: Angle / Primary Text / Headline (40 char) / Description (30 char) / CTA button / Audience temperature.

### 32. Meta Creative Brief Generator
**Prompt**: Act as a creative strategist at a 9-figure DTC ad agency. Write a Meta creative brief for [PRODUCT] targeting [AUDIENCE]. Output the standard Motion/Atria format: (1) creative concept title, (2) target persona one-liner, (3) hook (first 3 seconds), (4) body structure (problem/solution/proof/CTA), (5) on-screen text overlay script, (6) b-roll shot list, (7) suggested aspect ratios, (8) UGC vs studio recommendation, (9) 3 headline variants. Flag the #1 hypothesis being tested.

### 33. Facebook Ad Hook Library
**Prompt**: Act as a paid social copywriter specializing in first-line hooks that stop the scroll. For [PRODUCT] in the [NICHE] space, generate 25 first-line ad hooks (under 15 words each) across 5 categories: question, shocking stat, contrarian, personal confession, unexpected comparison. Output as a table: Category / Hook / Why It Stops Scroll / Best Audience Stage (cold/warm/hot). Then pick the top 3 to test first and explain the creative test plan over 2 weeks and a $500 budget.

### 34. UGC Ad Script (30 Seconds)
**Prompt**: Act as a UGC scriptwriter who has written ads for Ridge Wallet and Dr. Squatch. Write a 30-second UGC ad script for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]. Structure: Hook (0-3s), Problem setup (3-8s), Product reveal (8-15s), Benefit stack (15-22s), Social proof (22-27s), CTA (27-30s). Output as a 2-column table (Spoken VO / On-Screen Action) with timestamps. Include: 3 alternate hooks, 2 b-roll variations, text overlay copy, and the ad's single "memorable moment." Creator direction: speak conversationally.

### 35. Retargeting Ad Sequence
**Prompt**: Act as a full-funnel paid media strategist. Design a 4-stage retargeting ad sequence for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]: (1) 1-3 day post-visit (reminder), (2) 4-7 day (social proof), (3) 8-14 day (objection handler), (4) 15-30 day (discount/urgency). For each stage, output: audience definition, ad copy (125 words), headline, creative format recommendation, suggested CPM budget split. End with a flowchart of exit conditions (purchase, unsubscribe, 30-day window) and expected ROAS lift per stage.

### 36. Cold Audience Ad Copy
**Prompt**: Act as a direct-response media buyer who writes for cold Meta audiences. Write 3 long-form (300-word) ad bodies for [PRODUCT] targeting cold traffic [AUDIENCE]. Each must follow the "Story-Problem-Mechanism-Proof-Offer" arc used by Agora and ClickBank. No jargon, 6th-grade reading level. Output each with: hook first line, story section, mechanism reveal, 2 proof points, offer, CTA, headline 40 chars, description 30 chars. Recommend which angle to lead with based on market sophistication level.

### 37. Meta Ad Compliance Rewrite
**Prompt**: Act as a Meta ad compliance specialist who has appealed 500+ rejected ads. Rewrite [AD_COPY] to pass Meta's ad policies around personal attributes, health claims, and misleading assertions. Output: (1) original vs. rewritten side-by-side, (2) list of flagged phrases and safer replacements, (3) compliance confidence score 1-10, (4) a "hedging language library" for the [NICHE] vertical. Include what NOT to say explicitly (e.g., "you" phrases for health/finance) and the appeal template if rejected.

### 38. Carousel Ad Copy Template
**Prompt**: Act as a carousel ad copywriter for ecommerce brands. Design a 5-card carousel ad for [PRODUCT] at [PRICE]. Structure: Card 1 (hook/problem), Card 2 (benefit 1 with social proof), Card 3 (benefit 2), Card 4 (objection buster), Card 5 (offer + CTA). For each card, output: image direction, headline (40 char), description (30 char). Plus: primary text above the carousel (125 words) and 3 A/B test variations for Card 1 only. Recommend sequence for cold vs retargeting audiences.

### 39. Meta Ad Performance Analyzer
**Prompt**: Act as a performance creative analyst. Given these ad metrics [CTR, CPC, CPM, ROAS, Hook Rate, Hold Rate, Frequency] for [AD_NAME] running to [AUDIENCE] at [SPEND], diagnose what's broken. Output: (1) the single bottleneck (hook, body, offer, audience, creative fatigue), (2) evidence-based reasoning, (3) 3 test hypotheses to fix it ranked by expected impact, (4) new ad variant copy for the top hypothesis, (5) kill/scale/iterate decision framework. Include the specific metric threshold for each decision.

### 40. Whitelisted Creator Ad Brief
**Prompt**: Act as an influencer whitelisting strategist who has run Creator Ads for 8-figure brands. Write a creator brief for [CREATOR] in [NICHE] to post an ad for [PRODUCT] under whitelist rights. Include: hook direction (3 options), product talking points (5 max), prohibited claims, required disclosures, caption draft, do's/don'ts list, 3 reference ads, timeline, usage rights, and performance bonus structure. Output in a clean brief format a creator can execute without follow-up questions.

### 41. Google Search Ad RSA Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a Google Ads specialist who has managed $5M+ on search campaigns. Build a Responsive Search Ad for [PRODUCT] targeting keyword theme [KEYWORDS]. Output: 15 headlines (30 char max) covering brand, benefit, feature, CTA, urgency, social proof, price, location; 4 descriptions (90 char max) covering value prop, offer, trust, CTA. Pin 2 headlines strategically and explain why. Include 5 recommended sitelinks, 4 callouts, and 3 structured snippets. End with the expected Ad Strength rating.

### 42. Keyword Intent Mapping
**Prompt**: Act as a PPC strategist specializing in search intent. Given [KEYWORD_LIST] for [PRODUCT], classify each keyword into one of 4 intent buckets: informational, navigational, commercial investigation, transactional. For each bucket, recommend: match type, landing page, bid modifier, ad copy angle. Output as a table with columns: Keyword / Intent / Match Type / Landing Page / Bid Strategy / Ad Angle / Expected CPA. Flag negative keywords to add and explain the "money keyword" to protect with highest bid.

### 43. Google Ads Extension Pack
**Prompt**: Act as a Google Ads account manager who optimizes for high Ad Rank. For [BUSINESS] selling [PRODUCT], write a complete extensions package: 8 sitelinks (25 char + 2 description lines), 10 callouts (25 char), 8 structured snippets across 3 categories, 3 promotion extensions, 2 lead form extensions, and image extension shot direction. Output as a structured list grouped by extension type. Include the "don't duplicate ad copy" rule check and which extensions to prioritize for a $2K/month budget.

### 44. Shopping Ad Product Title Optimizer
**Prompt**: Act as a Google Shopping optimization specialist. Rewrite [CURRENT_PRODUCT_TITLE] following Google's title hierarchy for [PRODUCT_TYPE]: Brand + Product Type + Attributes (size, color, material, gender) + Model. Max 150 chars, optimize for search match. Output: (1) rewritten title, (2) 3 variants to A/B test, (3) top 5 attributes to include based on [CATEGORY] buying behavior, (4) title mistakes to avoid, (5) expected impression share lift. Include GTIN and MPN best practices.

### 45. Competitor Conquest Ad Strategy
**Prompt**: Act as a PPC growth hacker who runs competitor conquest campaigns ethically. For [OUR_BRAND] vs [COMPETITOR] in [CATEGORY], design a conquest campaign targeting competitor-brand keywords. Output: (1) trademark compliance checklist, (2) 10 ad headlines that contrast without using competitor's name in ad copy, (3) landing page framework for the "we vs them" page, (4) expected CPC premium and ROAS threshold to justify, (5) risk of retaliation scoring. Include a kill-switch metric.

### 46. Performance Max Asset Group
**Prompt**: Act as a Google Ads strategist specializing in Performance Max campaigns. Build a complete asset group for [PRODUCT] targeting [AUDIENCE_SIGNAL]. Output: 5 headlines (30 char), 5 long headlines (90 char), 5 descriptions (90 char), 1 business name, 1 call-to-action, 4 image direction briefs (landscape, square, portrait), 1 logo spec, 1 video script (15s). Include audience signal recommendations and the single ROAS target to set. Flag what happens if you don't give enough asset variety.

### 47. Local Services Ad Copy
**Prompt**: Act as a local PPC specialist for service businesses. Write Google Ads copy for [LOCAL_SERVICE] in [CITY]. Output: 15 headlines emphasizing location, trust (licensed/insured/years), urgency (same-day), social proof (reviews), price transparency; 4 descriptions; location extension text; call extension hours; lead form fields. Then write the landing page hero: H1 + subhead + 3 trust bullets + CTA + phone number placement. Include Google Business Profile tie-in recommendations.

### 48. Quality Score Recovery Plan
**Prompt**: Act as a Google Ads account auditor. Given [KEYWORD] with Quality Score of [X] and CTR of [Y]%, diagnose why QS is low across the 3 components: expected CTR, ad relevance, landing page experience. Output: (1) component scoring table, (2) 5 specific fixes prioritized by expected QS lift, (3) rewritten ad copy that matches query intent better, (4) landing page checklist, (5) 30-day QS recovery plan with weekly milestones. Include the CPC savings math if QS moves from [X] to 8.

### 49. Google Ads Negative Keyword Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a PPC waste-killer who has saved accounts 40%+ on irrelevant spend. For [PRODUCT] in [INDUSTRY], build a complete negative keyword list in 6 categories: informational ("how to," "what is"), DIY ("free," "template"), wrong intent ("jobs," "careers"), wrong audience ("kids," "wholesale"), competitor names, brand irrelevant. Output as 6 organized lists with match type recommendations (broad/phrase/exact). Include 20 negatives specific to [INDUSTRY] I wouldn't think of and the expected wasted-spend reduction.

### 50. YouTube Ads Hook Library

## 2 — Content Creation, Blogging & SEO
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> Keyword clustering · content briefs · on-page optimization · topical authority · technical SEO · YouTube scripts · newsletters · repurposing pipelines · link building · digital PR

---


### 1. Seed Keyword Expansion Matrix
**Prompt**: Act as a senior SEO strategist who has ranked 500+ pages on Google's first page for commercial keywords. Given seed keyword [SEED_KEYWORD] in the [NICHE] niche for audience [AUDIENCE], expand it into 50 related keywords using modifiers (informational, commercial, transactional, navigational), question-based variants, and long-tail versions. Output a markdown table with columns: Keyword, Search Intent, Estimated Monthly Volume, KD (0-100), Funnel Stage (TOFU/MOFU/BOFU), SERP Feature Opportunity.

### 2. Topical Authority Map Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a topical authority strategist trained on Koray Tugberk GUBUR's semantic SEO methodology. For the topic [PILLAR_TOPIC] targeting [AUDIENCE], build a complete topical map with 1 pillar page, 8 hub pages, and 40 spoke articles. For each node, specify: URL slug, primary keyword, search intent, parent node, internal linking targets, and entity coverage. Output as a nested JSON tree plus a markdown hierarchy diagram.

### 3. SERP Gap Analysis Framework
**Prompt**: Act as an Ahrefs-trained SEO analyst. Given target keyword [TARGET_KEYWORD] and top 10 ranking URLs [COMPETITOR_URLS], conduct a SERP gap analysis. Identify: (1) common H2 patterns across top 5, (2) entities/topics covered by 3+ competitors I must include, (3) content gaps nobody covers, (4) average word count, (5) schema types used, (6) SERP features present. Output as a structured brief with a "10x angle" recommendation at the end.

### 4. Skyscraper Content Upgrade Plan
**Prompt**: Act as Brian Dean and apply the Skyscraper Technique 2.0. Analyze the current top-ranking article [COMPETITOR_URL] for keyword [TARGET_KEYWORD]. Identify 5 weaknesses (outdated data, shallow examples, missing visuals, weak structure, thin E-E-A-T). Then outline a superior replacement article with: unique angle, updated 2026 data points, 3 original research ideas, proprietary frameworks, and an outreach list of 20 sites likely to link. Format as sections: Audit, Outline, Data Plan, Outreach Targets.

### 5. Keyword Clustering by Intent
**Prompt**: Act as a data-driven SEO consultant using keyword clustering via SERP overlap. ## 3 — Business Strategy, Entrepreneurship & Startups
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> Lean Canvas · Porter's 5 Forces · Blue Ocean · go-to-market · pricing models · financial modeling · pitch decks · investor memos · OKRs · hiring · org design

---


### 1. Lean Canvas Deep Build
**Prompt**: Act as a Lean Startup coach who has mentored 200+ YC and Techstars companies. For [COMPANY] targeting [CUSTOMER_SEGMENT] in [INDUSTRY], build a complete Lean Canvas. Stress-test each block against the Mom Test, flag the three riskiest assumptions, and propose a 2-week validation experiment per risk. Output as a 9-block Lean Canvas table followed by a "Risk & Experiment" matrix with hypothesis, metric, kill criteria, and cost.

### 2. Business Model Canvas Audit

Score each of the 9 blocks on a 1-5 coherence scale, identify structural misalignments between Value Proposition and Customer Segments, and propose three alternative BMC variants. Output as a scored BMC table plus a 2x2 "Impact vs Feasibility" matrix of variants.

### 3. Value Proposition Design

Identify the top 3 "fit gaps" and propose explicit pain-reliever redesigns. Output as a two-column VPC diagram in markdown plus a Fit Score table rating each job on evidence strength.

### 4. Jobs-to-be-Done Interview Kit

## 4 — Software Development & Engineering
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> System architecture · DDD · CQRS · event sourcing · SOLID refactoring · code review · debugging · TDD · API design · SQL tuning · Docker · Kubernetes · OWASP · iOS · React

---


### 1. Greenfield System Architecture
**Prompt**: Act as a principal software architect with 15 years designing distributed systems at Stripe and Shopify. I need to design [SYSTEM_DESCRIPTION] expecting [RPS] requests/sec and [DATA_VOLUME] of data. Propose a reference architecture covering compute, storage, caching, async messaging, and edge. Justify choices against CAP theorem trade-offs and 12-factor principles. Output: ASCII architecture diagram, component table (service, responsibility, tech, SLO), and 3 key risks with mitigations.

### 2. Monolith To Microservices Migration
**Prompt**: Act as a staff engineer who led 4 monolith decompositions at FAANG scale. My codebase is [CODEBASE_DESCRIPTION] with [LOC] lines in [LANGUAGE]. Propose a strangler-fig migration plan using DDD bounded contexts. Identify seams, shared kernels, and anti-corruption layers. Output: migration roadmap (6 phases), bounded-context map in ASCII, service extraction order ranked by risk/value, and rollback strategy per phase.

### 3. Event Driven Architecture Design

## 5 — AI, Automation & Productivity
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> Meta-prompting · chain-of-thought · tree-of-thought · ReAct · agentic workflows · GTD · inbox triage · meeting prep · second brain · Zapier & n8n blueprints · Feynman learning

---


### 1. Meta-Prompt Rewriter
**Prompt**: Act as a senior prompt engineer who has shipped production LLM agents at Anthropic scale. Take my raw prompt [INPUT_PROMPT] targeting [GOAL] and rewrite it using role-setting, explicit constraints [CONSTRAINTS], few-shot examples, and chain-of-thought scaffolding. Identify 3 ambiguity risks, 3 failure modes, and propose mitigations. Output as a markdown table with columns: Original, Rewritten, Rationale, Token Delta, Expected Quality Lift (1-10).

### 2. Few-Shot Example Generator
**Prompt**: Act as a prompt engineer specializing in in-context learning. For task [TASK_DESCRIPTION], generate 5 diverse few-shot examples covering edge cases, ambiguous inputs, and adversarial phrasing. Each example must show Input -> Reasoning -> Output. Use semantic diversity (not surface variations). Output as JSON array with fields: id, input, chain_of_thought, expected_output, difficulty (easy/medium/hard), edge_case_type.

### 3. Chain-of-Thought Scaffold
**Prompt**: Act as a reasoning systems researcher. Given problem [PROBLEM] with success metric [SUCCESS_METRIC], design a chain-of-thought scaffold that forces the model to: (1) decompose, (2) identify unknowns, (3) map to known patterns, (4) verify each step, (5) self-critique. Output as a reusable prompt template with [VARIABLES] and numbered thinking steps, plus a self-consistency voting rubric for N=5 samples.

### 4. Tree-of-Thought Planner
**Prompt**: Act as an AI agent architect implementing tree-of-thought reasoning. For decision [DECISION] with constraints [CONSTRAINTS], generate 3 branching strategies, evaluate each branch against [SUCCESS_METRIC] using a 1-10 rubric, prune dominated branches, then deepen the top branch two levels. Output as a markdown tree with evaluation scores, pruning rationale, and final recommended path with confidence interval.

### 5. ReAct Agent Blueprint
**Prompt**: Act as an agentic workflow designer. Build a ReAct (Reason + Act) loop for goal [GOAL] using tools [TOOLS_AVAILABLE]. Define: observation schema, reasoning template, action space, termination condition, max iterations, failure recovery. Include 2 worked examples showing Thought -> Action -> Observation -> Thought cycles. Output as a YAML config plus Python pseudocode for the agent loop with explicit state machine transitions.

### 6. Self-Consistency Voter
**Prompt**: Act as an LLM reliability engineer. Design a self-consistency pipeline for task [TASK] where N=5 reasoning samples are generated, normalized, then majority-voted. Specify: sampling temperature, normalization regex, tie-breaking rule, confidence threshold for escalation to human review. Output as a Python function signature with docstring, followed by a decision tree showing vote aggregation logic and abstention criteria.

### 7. Prompt Debugger
**Prompt**: Act as a prompt debugging specialist. My prompt [PROMPT] is producing output [ACTUAL_OUTPUT] but I expected [EXPECTED_OUTPUT]. Diagnose root cause using a 6-checkpoint framework: role clarity, instruction ordering, example quality, constraint conflicts, output format specification, implicit assumptions. Output as a diagnostic report with severity ratings, exact line-level fixes, and a regression test suite of 3 inputs to verify the fix.

### 8. System Prompt Architect
**Prompt**: Act as a system prompt architect for an AI product used by [USER_PERSONA] to accomplish [GOAL]. Design a system prompt covering: identity, capabilities, hard constraints, soft preferences, refusal policies, output format defaults, and escalation triggers. Keep under 500 tokens. Output as a numbered markdown spec plus the final compiled system prompt in a code block ready for API deployment.

### 9. Instruction Compression
**Prompt**: Act as a prompt optimization engineer focused on token efficiency. Compress my verbose prompt [INPUT_PROMPT] by 40-60% while preserving behavioral fidelity. Techniques allowed: remove hedging, consolidate redundant instructions, replace examples with schemas, use symbolic notation. Output original token count, compressed version, compressed token count, percentage reduction, and a behavioral equivalence checklist of 5 test inputs.

### 10. Prompt Evaluation Rubric
**Prompt**: Act as an LLM evaluation researcher. Build a prompt evaluation rubric for task [TASK_TYPE] scoring: correctness, completeness, format adherence, hallucination rate, instruction following, safety. Each dimension rated 1-5 with concrete anchors. Include inter-rater reliability guidance. Output as a markdown scorecard with rating anchors per dimension, aggregation formula, and a sample scored example showing how to apply the rubric.

### 11. Planner-Executor Split
**Prompt**: Act as an agentic systems architect. For complex goal [GOAL] requiring [TOOLS_AVAILABLE], split cognition across a planner LLM and executor LLM. Planner outputs a JSON plan with dependency graph; executor consumes subtasks and emits structured observations. Define interfaces, error handoff protocol, and replanning triggers. Output as 2 prompt templates (planner, executor) plus a message schema in JSON Schema format with required fields.

### 12. Tool Use Function Schemas
**Prompt**: Act as a function-calling API designer. ### 13. Multi-Agent Orchestration

### 50. Meeting ROI Calculator
**Prompt**: Act as a productivity economist. Given recurring meeting [MEETING] with [ATTENDEES] hourly rates averaging [RATE], duration [DURATION], and outcomes [OUTCOMES], compute cost per meeting, cost per decision, cost per action item produced. Benchmark against a 10x ROI threshold. Output as a cost-benefit table, a verdict (keep/shrink/kill), and 3 optimization levers ranked by savings potential with estimated dollar impact.

### 51. Project WBS Decomposer
**Prompt**: Act as a project manager certified in PMBOK. Decompose project [PROJECT] with goal [GOAL] into a work breakdown structure of at most 3 levels. Each leaf task must be 4-16 hours, have clear acceptance criteria, owner, dependencies, and effort estimate. Apply the 100% rule (children sum to parent). Output as an indented markdown tree plus a dependency graph in Mermaid syntax and a critical path highlight.

### 52. First Principles Decomposer
**Prompt**: Act as a first-principles thinker in the Elon Musk / Richard Feynman tradition. Given problem [PROBLEM], strip it to fundamental truths by asking "why" 5 times and "what must be true?" Identify assumptions, test each against physics/economics/logic, then rebuild a solution from atoms. Output as a 3-column table (Assumption, Challenge, First Principle) plus a reconstructed problem statement and a novel solution path.

### 53. MoSCoW Prioritizer
**Prompt**: Act as an agile product coach. Given backlog [BACKLOG] for sprint with capacity [CAPACITY], classify each item as Must/Should/Could/Won't using the MoSCoW method. For each Must, validate with the "release-breaking" test. For each Won't, add rationale for deferral. Output as a prioritized markdown table with effort estimates, cumulative capacity check, and a risk callout for any Musts exceeding 60% of capacity.

### 54. Pre-Mortem Analysis
**Prompt**: Act as a risk analyst running a Gary Klein-style pre-mortem. Imagine project [PROJECT] failed catastrophically 6 months from now. Brainstorm 15 plausible failure causes across 5 categories: technical, people, market, execution, external. Rank by likelihood x impact. For top 5, propose early warning indicators and mitigations. Output as a risk register with columns: Cause, Category, Likelihood (1-5), Impact (1-5), Signal, Mitigation, Owner.

### 55. Gantt Timeline Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a project scheduler. Given tasks [TASKS] with durations and dependencies [DEPENDENCIES], build a Gantt timeline starting [START_DATE] with a hard deadline [DEADLINE]. Apply critical path method, add 15% buffer, flag resource conflicts. Output as an ASCII Gantt chart, a critical path list, milestone dates, and a slippage playbook describing what to compress if the timeline slips by 1 week.

### 56. RACI Matrix Designer
**Prompt**: Act as an organizational design consultant. For project [PROJECT] with deliverables [DELIVERABLES] and stakeholders [STAKEHOLDERS], build a RACI matrix assigning Responsible, Accountable (exactly 1), Consulted, Informed. Apply validation rules: every deliverable has exactly one A, no person is over-allocated. Output as a markdown table with deliverables as rows, people as columns, plus a conflict report and redesign suggestions if any rule is violated.

### 57. User Story Writer
**Prompt**: Act as a senior product manager trained by Marty Cagan. For feature [FEATURE] serving user [PERSONA], write user stories using "As a [persona], I want [capability] so that [outcome]" plus Gherkin-format acceptance criteria (Given/When/Then). Include edge cases, error states, and non-functional requirements. Output as a user story card with title, narrative, 5 acceptance criteria, effort estimate, and definition-of-done checklist.

### 58. Scope Creep Defender
**Prompt**: Act as a project manager defending scope. Given original scope [ORIGINAL_SCOPE] and new request [NEW_REQUEST], run a scope impact analysis: does it serve the core goal? What gets delayed/cut? Estimate time/cost delta. Draft a stakeholder conversation script offering 3 options (absorb, trade-off, defer). Output as a scope change request form plus the verbal script with 3 pre-planned responses to pushback.

### 59. Dependency Mapper
**Prompt**: Act as a systems architect mapping project dependencies. Given tasks [TASKS], identify hard dependencies (must finish before), soft dependencies (preferred before), and parallel tracks. Detect cycles, bottlenecks, and single points of failure. Output as a directed graph in Mermaid syntax, a topological sort of execution order, a list of "unblocker" tasks that free the most downstream work, and a parallelization recommendation.

### 60. Milestone Retrospective
**Prompt**: Act as a project postmortem facilitator. Given completed milestone [MILESTONE] with data [ACTUAL_VS_PLAN], diagnose variance using the 5 Whys on any estimate miss greater than 20%. Extract lessons across people/process/tools. Output as a postmortem report with: timeline, key events, what went well, what didn't, root causes, action items with owners and due dates, and 3 process improvements to propagate to future projects.

### 61. Zettelkasten Atomizer
**Prompt**: Act as a knowledge management coach trained in the Zettelkasten method of Niklas Luhmann. Given source note [SOURCE_NOTE], atomize it into 3-7 permanent notes, each capturing exactly one idea in my own words, with a unique ID (YYYYMMDDHHMM), a descriptive title, and explicit [[wiki-links]] to related notes. Output as markdown files ready for Obsidian with frontmatter, body under 300 words each, and a link section suggesting 3 connections.

### 62. Second Brain PARA Setup
**Prompt**: Act as a productivity coach certified in Tiago Forte's Building a Second Brain. Given my current information chaos [CURRENT_STATE], design a PARA structure (Projects, Areas, Resources, Archive) for Notion/Obsidian. Define: what belongs where, capture workflow (progressive summarization), weekly maintenance ritual. Output as a folder tree, naming conventions, a CODE method checklist (Capture-Organize-Distill-Express), and a 14-day onboarding plan.

### 63. Obsidian Graph Builder
**Prompt**: Act as an Obsidian power user. Given my notes on topic [TOPIC], design an MOC (Map of Content) note that serves as a curated entry point, plus suggested tags, dataview queries for dynamic sections, and a template for note frontmatter. Output as a ready-to-paste MOC markdown file with sections, inline dataview queries in code blocks, and 3 canvas layout suggestions for visual thinking.

### 64. Smart Note Taking
**Prompt**: Act as a researcher applying Sonke Ahrens' "How to Take Smart Notes". Given source [SOURCE], produce: fleeting notes (quick captures), literature notes (bibliographic summary in my words under 200 words), and permanent notes (atomic insights with links). Distinguish reference, claim, and my original thought. Output as 3 markdown sections with clear boundaries, citation in plain text, and 2 questions the source opens up.

### 65. Progressive Summarization
**Prompt**: Act as a knowledge distillation engineer. Given article [ARTICLE], apply 4 layers of progressive summarization: (1) highlight key passages, (2) bold the most important, (3) italicize the core claim, (4) write a 3-sentence executive summary. Each layer reduces by ~5x. Output as the full article with layer 1-3 markup preserved, followed by the level 4 summary and 1 "so what" action implication.

### 66. Literature Review Synthesizer
**Prompt**: Act as a PhD research assistant. Given papers [PAPERS] on topic [TOPIC], produce a literature review synthesizing: shared framings, points of disagreement, gaps in the field, methodological patterns, and open questions. Use thematic clustering, not chronological ordering. Output as a 500-word review with inline citations, a comparison matrix of papers on 5 dimensions, and 3 research questions worth pursuing next.

### 67. Knowledge Graph Query
**Prompt**: Act as a knowledge graph architect. Given my note corpus [CORPUS] and question [QUESTION], design a graph traversal that surfaces relevant notes via tag intersection, backlink density, and semantic similarity. Output as a pseudocode query, a ranked list of top 10 relevant notes with relevance scores and rationale, and a synthesis paragraph answering the question grounded in those notes with inline [[links]].

### 68. Daily Note Template
**Prompt**: Act as a journaling coach combining Bullet Journal and Morning Pages practices. Design a daily note template for Obsidian containing: 3-sentence intention, top 3 tasks, time log, gratitudes, wins, what I learned, tomorrow's focus, mood 1-10, energy 1-10. Include dataview queries to pull today's tasks from project notes. Output as a markdown template with frontmatter, sections, and inline queries ready to use in a daily note plugin.

### 69. Flashcard Generator
**Prompt**: Act as a learning scientist building spaced repetition decks. Given source material [SOURCE], generate 15 Anki-style flashcards using the minimum information principle (one fact per card), avoiding verbatim copying. Mix cloze deletions, Q&A, and image occlusion suggestions. Output as a CSV with columns Front, Back, Tags, Type, plus 3 sample cards in markdown preview showing front/back and a difficulty rating per card.

### 70. Commonplace Book Entry
**Prompt**: Act as Ryan Holiday's commonplace book curator. Given passage [PASSAGE] from author [AUTHOR], craft a commonplace entry containing: the quote verbatim, source citation, my paraphrase in plain language, 1 personal connection, 1 actionable principle, and 3 tags for future retrieval. Output as a markdown note with YAML frontmatter suitable for Obsidian, body under 300 words, and a "future trigger" note describing when to recall this.

### 71. Pros Cons Matrix
**Prompt**: Act as a decision analyst. For decision [DECISION] between options [OPTION_A] and [OPTION_B], build a weighted pros/cons matrix: list factors, assign weights (1-10) based on my values [VALUES], score each option per factor (-5 to +5), compute weighted totals. Include gut-check via premortem and reversibility test (one-way vs two-way door). Output as a markdown table, weighted score, and a narrative recommendation.

### 72. Decision Journal Entry
**Prompt**: Act as a decision coach trained on Annie Duke's "Thinking in Bets". For upcoming decision [DECISION], draft a decision journal entry capturing: situation, options considered, option chosen, expected outcome with probability, alternative I rejected and why, emotional state, what would change my mind. Output as a structured journal entry template in markdown with YAML frontmatter (date, stakes, confidence) for future review and learning.

### 73. Red Team Critique
**Prompt**: Act as a hostile red team attacking my plan [PLAN]. Steel-man 5 critiques: is the premise wrong? Is the evidence weak? Are assumptions hidden? Is the execution path flawed? What does the smartest opponent say? Be brutally honest, not polite. Output as 5 numbered critiques, each with: claim, evidence, severity (1-5), and a specific action I should take to address or dismiss the critique.

### 74. Inversion Thinking
**Prompt**: Act as Charlie Munger applying inversion. For goal [GOAL], flip the question: instead of "how do I achieve this?" ask "how would I guarantee failure?" Enumerate 10 failure paths, then invert each into an avoidance rule. Output as a 2-column table (Failure Path, Avoidance Rule) plus a top-3 priority list of avoidance rules ranked by likelihood and a daily checklist question to keep me aligned.

### 75. Opportunity Cost Calculator
**Prompt**: Act as an economist applying opportunity cost reasoning. Given choice [CHOICE] requiring time investment [TIME] and money [MONEY], enumerate the next 3 best alternatives, estimate their expected value, and compute opportunity cost as value forgone. Apply the "hell yes or no" filter from Derek Sivers. Output as a comparison table, an opportunity cost figure in dollars and hours, and a decision recommendation with confidence.

### 76. Second Order Thinking
**Prompt**: Act as Howard Marks applying second- and third-order thinking. For action [ACTION], trace consequences across orders: first (immediate), second (reactions), third (systemic), fourth (long tail). For each order, identify stakeholder reactions and feedback loops. Output as a cascading markdown outline with orders as headers, consequences as bullets, and a summary of "what most people miss" plus a decision modifier if any order reveals hidden risk.

### 77. Expected Value Calculator
**Prompt**: Act as a poker player applying expected value math. Given bet [BET] with outcomes [OUTCOMES], probabilities [PROBABILITIES], and payoffs [PAYOFFS], compute EV, variance, and Kelly criterion bet size relative to bankroll [BANKROLL]. Apply the "resulting" check (good decision vs good outcome). Output as a calculation table, a narrative explaining whether the bet is +EV, and a recommended action with position sizing.

### 78. Moral Compass Check
**Prompt**: Act as an ethics advisor applying multiple frameworks. For dilemma [DILEMMA], evaluate under 4 lenses: consequentialism (outcomes), deontology (duties), virtue ethics (character), care ethics (relationships). Note where they converge and diverge. Output as a 4-column analysis plus a reconciled recommendation with the dominant framework justified, a "stranger test" (would I be comfortable if this were front-page news), and a reversibility clause.

### 79. Pre-Commitment Device
**Prompt**: Act as a behavioral economist in the Ulysses contract tradition. Given temptation [TEMPTATION] that undermines goal [GOAL], design a pre-commitment device: stake (money, reputation), referee, verification method, reward/punishment schedule, exit conditions. Tools: Beeminder, StickK, accountability partner. Output as a contract document with stake amount, verification rule, weekly check-in schedule, and an "if-then" escape clause for legitimate exceptions.

### 80. Sunk Cost Escape
**Prompt**: Act as a rationality coach identifying sunk cost fallacy. Given commitment [COMMITMENT] with [SUNK_INVESTMENT] already spent, evaluate forward-only: if I were starting today with current information, would I make this investment? Apply the "freshman year" test. Output as a 3-step analysis (forget past, assess present, project future EV), a verdict (continue/quit/pivot), and a narrative script to communicate the decision to stakeholders.

### 81. Zapier Workflow Blueprint
**Prompt**: Act as an automation architect specializing in Zapier. Design a zap for goal [GOAL] connecting [APPS]. Specify: trigger, filters, paths, formatter steps, action apps, error handling, testing plan. Estimate task consumption per month. Output as a step-by-step blueprint in a numbered list, field-level mapping for the first and last step, a JSON-like pseudocode of the workflow, and a cost estimate on the relevant Zapier plan.

### 82. n8n Node Chain
**Prompt**: Act as an n8n workflow engineer. Build a workflow for [TASK] using trigger [TRIGGER] and actions [ACTIONS]. Specify: node types, expressions for data mapping (JavaScript), conditional branches (IF nodes), error workflow, credentials required. Self-host recommendation if volume is high. Output as a numbered node list with expressions, a JSON export snippet for the key nodes, and a test payload to verify the workflow end-to-end.

### 83. Make Scenario Design
**Prompt**: Act as a Make.com (Integromat) power user. Design a scenario automating [PROCESS] with modules [MODULES]. Use aggregators, iterators, routers, data stores. Specify operation cost, error handlers, scheduling. Output as a module-by-module spec with connection notes, a flow diagram in ASCII showing routers and aggregators, an operation count estimate, and 3 optimization tips to reduce operations consumed per run.

### 84. Apple Shortcuts Recipe
**Prompt**: Act as an Apple Shortcuts power user. Build a Shortcut for [TASK] usable from Siri, Share Sheet, or Widget. Use actions: Get Contents of URL, Scripting, Conditional, Dictionary. Include a settings variable for customization. Output as a step-by-step action list with parameters, a test case, the Siri phrase to invoke, a home-screen icon suggestion, and a fallback if a required service is unavailable.

### 85. Raycast Script Command
**Prompt**: Act as a Raycast extension developer. Build a script command in Bash or Node.js for task [TASK] with arguments [ARGS]. Follow Raycast conventions: schema version, title, mode (silent/fullOutput/inline), refreshTime. Handle errors gracefully. Output as the full script file content with the required metadata comment header, error handling, a usage example, and installation instructions for dropping into ~/.config/raycast/scripts.

### 86. Cron + Shell Pipeline
**Prompt**: Act as a devops engineer scheduling a daily automation. For task [TASK], write a shell script that runs reliably from cron on macOS/Linux: PATH handling, logging with timestamp, lock file to prevent overlap, failure alerts via email or webhook. Output as a complete bash script with shebang, a crontab line specifying schedule, a logrotate suggestion, and a manual test command with expected output.

### 87. GitHub Actions Workflow
**Prompt**: Act as a CI/CD engineer writing a GitHub Actions workflow for task [TASK] triggered on [TRIGGER]. Include: matrix builds, caching, secrets management, concurrency control, artifact upload, failure notifications. Output as a complete workflow YAML file saved to .github/workflows/[name].yml with comments explaining each step, a test branch strategy, and a cost estimate in minutes per month under normal load.

### 88. iOS Shortcuts Automation
**Prompt**: Act as an iOS automation expert. Build a personal automation triggered by [TRIGGER] (time, arrival, app open, focus mode) that performs [ACTIONS]. Use Shortcuts' Automation tab, not manual invocation. Include guard conditions to avoid spam. Output as a step-by-step action list, trigger configuration, test plan, and a privacy note on what data the automation accesses plus a disable/snooze plan for edge cases.

### 89. Webhook Middleware Design
**Prompt**: Act as a serverless architect. Design a webhook middleware that receives events from [SOURCE] and dispatches to [DESTINATIONS]. Use Cloudflare Workers, Deno Deploy, or AWS Lambda. Handle: signature verification, idempotency, retries with exponential backoff, dead letter queue. Output as a pseudocode function, the endpoint contract in OpenAPI snippet form, a retry policy table, and an alerting rule for the DLQ hitting a threshold.

### 90. RSS to Action Pipeline
**Prompt**: Act as a content automation engineer. Build a pipeline that watches RSS feed [FEED] for keyword [KEYWORD] and triggers action [ACTION] (email, Notion page, Slack message). Use RSS.app, n8n, or a cron Python script. Include dedupe via GUID store. Output as a workflow blueprint with components, a Python implementation skeleton (50 lines), state storage schema, and a backfill strategy for the first run.

### 91. Feynman Technique Coach
**Prompt**: Act as a Feynman Technique coach. I want to learn [TOPIC] by teaching it to a 12-year-old. Step 1: ask me 5 probing questions to find gaps in my current understanding. Step 2: grade my explanation attempt [ATTEMPT] on simplicity, accuracy, and analogy quality. Step 3: point to exactly where I leaned on jargon and suggest plain-language alternatives. Output as a graded rubric plus a rewritten 200-word explanation.

### 92. Spaced Repetition Planner
**Prompt**: Act as a learning scientist applying SM-2 spaced repetition to material [MATERIAL]. Given my study time [DAILY_MINUTES] and deadline [DEADLINE], build a review schedule across 7 intervals (1d, 3d, 7d, 14d, 30d, 60d, 120d). Include new-card introduction rate and retention target. Output as a daily schedule table for the next 30 days with cards to review, cards to introduce, and estimated time per session.

### 93. Skill Roadmap Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a skill acquisition coach applying Josh Kaufman's "First 20 Hours" and K. Anders Ericsson's deliberate practice. Given target skill [SKILL] and current level [LEVEL], build a 20-hour roadmap with: decomposition into sub-skills, order of learning by leverage, practice drills with feedback loops, plateaus to expect. Output as a milestone-based plan, a daily drill template, and a self-assessment rubric with 5 levels.

### 94. Learning Contract
**Prompt**: Act as a self-directed learning coach applying Malcolm Knowles' andragogy. For goal [LEARNING_GOAL] over period [TIMEFRAME], draft a learning contract covering: objectives, resources, strategies, evidence of completion, evaluation criteria. Include an accountability partner clause and a weekly reflection prompt. Output as a signed-ready contract document in markdown with sections, measurable outcomes, and a midpoint checkpoint review plan.

### 95. Deliberate Practice Session
**Prompt**: Act as a deliberate practice coach. Design a 60-minute practice session for skill [SKILL] at level [LEVEL]. Include: warm-up (5 min), targeted drill on weakness [WEAKNESS] (30 min) with immediate feedback loops, integration exercise (15 min), cool-down reflection (10 min). Output as a timed session plan with drill specifications, success criteria per segment, a feedback capture template, and the next session's focus area based on today's results.

### 96. Reading Note Protocol
**Prompt**: Act as a power reader applying Mortimer Adler's "How to Read a Book". For book [BOOK], run the 4 levels: elementary (scan), inspectional (preview TOC and conclusions), analytical (structured notes), syntopical (compare with other books on the topic). Output as a pre-read 15-minute inspection note, a reading plan with time budget per chapter, and a template for analytical notes with pillars: structure, key claims, evidence, objections.

### 97. Question-Led Learning
**Prompt**: Act as a Socratic tutor. I want to learn [TOPIC] by answering questions rather than consuming content. Generate a 10-question curriculum from beginner to expert, each question designed to force a concept discovery, with a hint unlocked after 2 minutes of thinking. Output as a numbered question list, difficulty progression, hint bank, and a self-grading rubric for when I should move to the next question.

### 98. Teaching Doc Generator
**Prompt**: Act as a technical writer. Transform my rough notes on [TOPIC] into a teaching document for audience [AUDIENCE]. Use the "inverted pyramid" plus Diataxis framework: is this a tutorial, how-to, explanation, or reference? Structure accordingly. Output as a markdown document with TOC, prerequisites, learning outcomes, worked example, exercises with solutions, further reading, and a self-check quiz of 5 questions.

### 99. Mental Model Index Builder
**Prompt**: Act as a polymath building a personal mental model latticework in the Munger tradition. Given my field [FIELD] and current models [CURRENT_MODELS], identify 10 high-leverage models missing from my latticework across disciplines (physics, biology, economics, psychology, math). For each, provide: 1-sentence definition, when to apply, canonical example, link to related models. Output as an indexed markdown database ready for Obsidian.

### 100. Meta-Learning Retrospective
**Prompt**: Act as a meta-learning coach. Over the last month I learned [WHAT] via [METHOD] with results [RESULTS]. Diagnose what worked, what wasted time, and which techniques to double down on. Apply Scott Young's ultralearning principles (directness, drill, feedback, retrieval). Output as a meta-learning retrospective report with: method scorecard, time audit, retention check via recall test, and a revised learning protocol for the next month with 3 experiments.
## 6 — Writing, Editing & Storytelling
### 100 Expert Prompts Inside

> 3-act structure · Save the Cat · Hero's Journey · character arcs · dialogue · worldbuilding · memoir · developmental editing · line edits · poetry · screenwriting

---


### 1. Three-Act Structure Blueprint
**Prompt**: Act as a developmental editor at a Big 5 publishing house who has shaped three NYT bestsellers. Using the classic 3-act structure, outline a [GENRE] novel starring [PROTAGONIST] facing [CONFLICT] in [SETTING]. Identify the inciting incident, first plot point, midpoint reversal, crisis, climax, and resolution with page-count targets for a [WORD_COUNT] manuscript. Output as a labeled beat-by-beat table with one-sentence purpose statements for each beat.

### 2. Save the Cat Beat Sheet
**Prompt**: Act as a story consultant trained in Blake Snyder's Save the Cat! method who has doctored six produced screenplays. Build a full 15-beat Save the Cat beat sheet for a [GENRE] story about [PROTAGONIST] whose flaw is [FLAW] and whose external goal is [GOAL]. Specify the theme stated, debate, break into two, fun and games, bad guys close in, dark night of the soul, and finale. Output as a numbered beat sheet with page targets and emotional temperature notes.

### 3. Hero's Journey Deconstruction
**Prompt**: Act as a mythologist in the Joseph Campbell tradition with a PhD in comparative literature. Map a [GENRE] story featuring [PROTAGONIST] onto all 12 stages of the Hero's Journey, from ordinary world through return with the elixir. For each stage, specify the external event, internal shift, and symbolic object or threshold guardian. Avoid cliche fantasy tropes; force fresh choices rooted in [THEME]. Output as a 12-row table: Stage, External Event, Internal Shift, Symbol.

### 4. Dan Harmon Story Circle
**Prompt**: Act as a veteran TV writers' room head who has staffed on prestige dramas for HBO. Apply Dan Harmon's 8-step Story Circle (You, Need, Go, Search, Find, Take, Return, Change) to a pilot episode of a [GENRE] series starring [PROTAGONIST] in [SETTING]. Make the Need and Change genuinely transformative, not cosmetic. Output as 8 paragraphs, one per step, each 60-80 words, with the thematic question named upfront.

### 5. Snowflake Method Expansion
**Prompt**: Act as a novelist trained in Randy Ingermanson's Snowflake Method. Expand a one-sentence logline about [PROTAGONIST] and [CONFLICT] into the first five Snowflake steps: one-sentence summary, paragraph summary, character sheets, one-page synopsis, and four-page synopsis. Keep disasters on-pattern (three disasters plus ending). Output each step in its own labeled section, with word counts noted. Preserve causal logic between disasters.

### 6. Freytag's Pyramid Analysis
**Prompt**: Act as a dramaturg who has staged Chekhov and Ibsen at regional theaters. Using Freytag's pyramid, plot a [GENRE] story starring [PROTAGONIST] across exposition, rising action, climax, falling action, and denouement. Identify the precise turning point ("peripeteia") and the moment of recognition ("anagnorisis"). Avoid modern 3-act conflation. Output as a five-section breakdown with a one-line function statement and the emotional register for each section.

### 7. Midpoint Reversal Engineering
**Prompt**: Act as a story doctor who has rescued three stalled [GENRE] manuscripts for agents at ICM. Design a midpoint reversal for a story about [PROTAGONIST] pursuing [GOAL] that flips the stakes from external to internal, reframes the antagonist, and forces the protagonist from reactive to proactive. Output: (1) the current midpoint sketch, (2) three alternative midpoints ranked by dramatic torque, (3) the ripple effects each creates in act three.

### 8. Subplot Weaving System
**Prompt**: Act as a narrative architect who has edited tangled multi-POV fantasy novels. Generate three interlocking subplots for a [GENRE] novel whose A-plot concerns [MAIN_CONFLICT]. Each subplot must (a) thematically echo the main story, (b) intersect the A-plot at two specific beats, and (c) resolve with tonal contrast. Output as a table: Subplot, Theme Echo, Intersection Points, Resolution Tone, POV Character.

### 9. Logline Surgery
**Prompt**: Act as a Hollywood script consultant who has pitched at Sundance Labs. Take this rough logline: "[ROUGH_LOGLINE]" and rewrite it three ways, each under 35 words, using the formula: protagonist + inciting event + goal + antagonist + stakes + irony. Rank the three versions by marketability, then explain in 40 words which cliches you eliminated. Output as numbered loglines followed by a ranked rationale.

### 10. Plot Hole Stress Test
**Prompt**: Act as a continuity editor who has caught plot holes for Peter Jackson and Christopher Nolan. Read this [WORD_COUNT] outline of a [GENRE] story and run a logic stress test. Flag every causal gap, unearned coincidence, character-knowledge contradiction, and timeline inconsistency. Output as a numbered list: Issue, Location, Why It Breaks, Suggested Patch. Prioritize fixes that require minimal rewriting while preserving thematic intent.

### 11. Character Want vs Need
**Prompt**: Act as a character coach who has developed protagonists for Pixar's story department. For [PROTAGONIST] in a [GENRE] story, articulate the surface "want" (concrete, external, pursuable) versus the hidden "need" (emotional, often opposed to the want). Explain how the climax forces a choice between them. Output as: Want (one sentence), Need (one sentence), Lie They Believe, Climactic Crossroads (80 words).

### 12. Character Flaw Cartography
**Prompt**: Act as a psychologically-trained novelist in the tradition of Donna Tartt. Design a three-layer flaw structure for [PROTAGONIST]: (1) the surface flaw readers notice in chapter one, (2) the psychological wound that caused it, (3) the moral flaw that will cost them in act three. Anchor each layer in a specific backstory beat. Output as three labeled paragraphs of 70-90 words each, plus one "ghost from the past" vignette.

### 13. Backstory Iceberg
**Prompt**: Act as a literary novelist trained at the Iowa Writers' Workshop. Build a backstory iceberg for [CHARACTER] where only the top 10% surfaces on the page. Generate 15 backstory facts ordered from most buried (childhood trauma, secret shame) to nearly visible (recent regret). Mark which three facts the reader should infer without being told. Output as a numbered list with a "reveal strategy" column: Shown, Implied, Withheld.

### 14. Antagonist Humanization
**Prompt**: Act as a villain whisperer who has consulted on HBO prestige dramas. Take the villain [ANTAGONIST] from a [GENRE] story and write their internal monologue for the moment just before their worst act. They must be the hero of their own story. Avoid mustache-twirling. Include one concrete sensory detail, one justified belief, and one flicker of doubt. Output as 180-220 words of first-person close POV.

### 15. Character Arc Ladder
**Prompt**: Act as a story structure expert in the K.M. Weiland tradition. Design a positive change arc ladder for [PROTAGONIST] across a [WORD_COUNT] novel. Identify the Lie Believed, the Truth to be discovered, the Ghost event, and six specific scene-level rungs where belief shifts. Output as a numbered ladder: Rung, Scene Premise, Old Belief Weakening, New Belief Strengthening. End with the climactic moment of full integration.

### 16. Ensemble Cast Differentiation
**Prompt**: Act as a showrunner who has balanced ensemble casts on shows like The Wire. Given an ensemble of six characters in a [GENRE] story, assign each a distinct want, need, flaw, secret, speech pattern, and physical tell. Ensure no two characters occupy the same narrative function. Output as a 6-row character bible table. Append a 60-word note on how their goals will clash in the season finale.

### 17. Foil Character Construction
**Prompt**: Act as a classicist who teaches character doubling at a top MFA program. Design a foil character for [PROTAGONIST] who inverts their strengths and exposes their weaknesses without being a mere opposite. The foil must share one core value but diverge on method. Give them a distinct voice, backstory, and thematic function. Output as a comparison chart (Trait, Protagonist, Foil) followed by a 100-word scene sketch of their first confrontation.

### 18. Character Introduction Moment
**Prompt**: Act as the screenwriter of a Best Picture Oscar winner known for iconic character entrances. Write the introduction scene for [CHARACTER] in a [GENRE] story, using Blake Snyder's "Save the Cat" principle to earn sympathy in 250 words. Show their occupation, flaw, and a hint of their secret without on-the-nose dialogue. Reveal character through action, not exposition. Output as a prose scene with a one-line thematic tag at the end.

### 19. Internal Monologue Calibration
**Prompt**: Act as a close-third POV specialist who edits literary fiction for Knopf. Rewrite this paragraph: "[PARAGRAPH]" to deepen the interiority of [CHARACTER]. Interweave sensory observation, associative memory, and unspoken judgment so the reader inhabits the character's mind without italics or thought-tags. Preserve plot content. Output the revised paragraph, then list five specific interiority techniques you applied.

### 20. Character Voice Audit
**Prompt**: Act as a voice coach for novelists, trained by George Saunders. Audit the voice of [CHARACTER] across these three sample passages: "[SAMPLE_1]", "[SAMPLE_2]", "[SAMPLE_3]". Identify their diction register, sentence rhythm, favored syntactic structures, vocabulary ceiling, and verbal tics. Flag any inconsistencies across samples. Output as a Voice Profile (200 words) followed by five diagnostic questions to sharpen the voice further.

### 21. Dialogue Subtext Layering
**Prompt**: Act as a dialogue doctor who has punched up scripts for Aaron Sorkin. Rewrite this on-the-nose exchange: "[EXCHANGE]" so every line says one thing and means another. Characters should talk around the real topic, using evasion, deflection, and micro-aggression. Preserve the plot information conveyed. Output the rewritten dialogue (10-14 lines), then annotate each line with the subtext in brackets.

### 22. Character-Specific Cadence
**Prompt**: Act as a linguistic stylist who has coached voice actors for HBO audiobooks. Generate 12 lines of dialogue for [CHARACTER], whose background is [BACKGROUND] and whose emotional state is [STATE]. Use consistent sentence-length rhythm, idiolect, and one signature filler. Ensure the reader could identify the speaker blindfolded. Output as dialogue lines without tags, followed by a 50-word style note explaining the rhythmic choices.

### 23. Differentiating Two Voices
**Prompt**: Act as a dialogue editor for prestige TV. Write a 20-line exchange between two characters of the same age, class, and region who must still sound clearly distinct. Use syntactic contrast (hypotactic vs paratactic), different pet words, and contrasting listening styles (one interrupts, one pauses). Output as a stage-play-formatted exchange, then append a 60-word note on the three differentiators you engineered.

### 24. Argument Without Shouting
**Prompt**: Act as a playwright in the Annie Baker tradition. Write a tense argument between [CHARACTER_A] and [CHARACTER_B] over [TOPIC] without a single raised voice, exclamation mark, or insult. Use pauses, shifts in formality, and strategic silence to escalate stakes. Keep it under 300 words. Output as script-formatted dialogue with parenthetical stage directions only where essential to breath and body.

### 25. Exposition Via Conflict
**Prompt**: Act as a narrative efficiency expert who doctors bloated novel openings. Take this exposition dump: "[EXPOSITION]" and convert it into a dialogue scene where two characters reveal the same information through a disagreement with opposing stakes. The reader must absorb the facts without noticing them being delivered. Output the scene (200-280 words) plus a bullet list of which facts landed where.

### 26. Regional Dialect Without Cliche
**Prompt**: Act as a dialect coach who worked on True Detective and The Wire. Write 15 lines of dialogue for a character from [REGION] that captures authentic rhythm, grammar, and vocabulary without resorting to phonetic respelling or eye-dialect. ### 27. Silence and Beat Work
**Prompt**: Act as a scene director trained at Steppenwolf. Take this dialogue exchange: "[EXCHANGE]" and rewrite it inserting six beats of physical business, silence, or environmental interruption that do the emotional heavy lifting instead of the lines. Beats must reveal character, not just decorate. Output the rewritten scene in screenplay format with parentheticals for beats, followed by a 50-word director's note.

### 28. Multilingual Dialogue Styling
**Prompt**: Act as a bilingual novelist in the Junot Diaz tradition. Write a scene in which [CHARACTER] code-switches between English and [LANGUAGE] without italics, glossing, or translation footnotes. Context must carry meaning for monolingual readers while rewarding bilingual ones. Keep it 250 words. Output as prose with integrated dialogue, then append a 60-word craft note on how you handled translation.

### 29. Interior Dialogue vs Speech
**Prompt**: Act as a literary editor who specializes in close POV. Write a scene where [CHARACTER] engages in polite dinner conversation while their interior monologue rages in a completely different register. Show the gap between surface and private voice. Keep surface dialogue restrained; interior should be wild, associative, metaphoric. Output as alternating speech (in quotes) and interior (in italics) for roughly 300 words.

### 30. Phone Call Reconstruction
**Prompt**: Act as a screenwriter who specializes in one-sided phone dialogue. Write a 250-word scene in which [CHARACTER] takes a life-altering phone call. We hear only their side. The reader must infer the full shape of the other conversation from pauses, reactions, and repetitions. Avoid obvious "wait, what?" constructions. Output as prose with dialogue, ending on the moment just after the call ends.

### 31. Opening Line Workshop

### 32. Scene Tension Escalation

Output the revised scene (350-450 words) with a charge-tracker appendix showing the emotional polarity at each beat.

### 33. Sensory Detail Layering

### 37. Quiet Scene Craft

### 38. Chase Sequence Pacing

### 40. Scene Cut and Transition
